<p>If a word is an adverb (not derived), conjunction, interjection or preposition, this is shown by {adv.}, {konj.}, {interj.} or {prep.}.</p>
<p>Similarly, a prefix is indicated with {pref.}, and a suffix with {suf.}.</p>
<p>Verbs: {tr} = transitive; {ntr} = intransitive; {tr/ntr} = both transitive and intransitive; {imp} = impersonal (needing no subject).</p>
<p>The abbreviation "Ant:" precedes an antonym.</p>
<p>An obsolete word has a bracket before it, and is followed by "<i>(obs.)</i>", a chevron and the word by which it was replaced.</p>
<p>A list of abbreviations is given at the end of the vocabulary.</p>

<p>Se vorto esas adverbo (ne derivita), interjeciono, konjunciono o prepoziciono, to esas indikata da {adv.}, {interj.}, {konj.} o {prep.}.</p>
<p>Simile, prefixo indikesas da {pref.}, e sufixo da {suf.}.</p>
<p>Verbi: {tr} = transitiva; {ntr} = netransitiva; {tr/ntr} = transitiva e netransitiva; {imp} = nepersonala (sen subjekto).</p>
<p>Vorti inter kramponi, pos verbo, esas vorti qui normale esas uzata pos ta verbo.</p>
<p>La abreviuro "Ant:" sequesas da antonimo.</p>
<p>Obsoleta vorto havas krampono avan ol, ed esas sequata da "<i>(obs.)</i>", chevrono e la nuna vorto qua remplasis ol.</p>
<p>Listo di abreviuri esas ye la fino di la lexiko.</p>
